2008-05-19 17:39 +0000 [r809879-809883] David Nolden <david.nolden.kde art-master.de>
language/duchain/classfunctiondeclaration.cpp
language/duchain/duchainlock.cpp
language/duchain/ducontext.cpp,
language/duchain/topducontext.cpp, language/duchain/ducontext.h,
language/duchain/topducontext.h
Output something instead of crashing on the assertion.
Increase the timeout. When something takes long it's painful, but when it
makes kdevelop crash that's even more painful.
Optimizations to the import-structure stuff: - Allow doing "temporary"
imports, which is imports that are not recursively propagated into
importers(needed in C++). - Do not maintain the shortest path for now, it's
too slow in very complicated cases. Any path is ok. - Do not compute the
recursive imports until they are requested for the first time. This saves us
from expensive computations where it's not needed. - Add mechanisms to import
and unimport multiple contexts at a time, for speedup. All this stuff has a
test in kdevelop, and it still succeeds.

2008-05-06 09:11 +0000 [r804503] Vladimir Prus <ghost cs.msu.su>
shell/mainwindow_p.cpp, shell/mainwindow_p.h
Fix xmlgui crashes when closing views. We failed to remove XMLGUIClient for
Kate views when closing those views. As result KXMLGUIFactory used to hold on
to deleted clients, and when we eventually created new view and tried to
switch to it, "removing" old, already-deleted, one, things would crash. Or not
crash, depending on luck, but usually, 10 attempts at opening/closing view
were sufficient for segfault to appear.

2008-04-27 19:46 +0000 [r801798] Alexander Dymo <adymo kdevelop.org>
shell/partdocument.cpp, interfaces/idocument.h,
shell/textdocument.h, shell/partcontroller.cpp,
shell/partdocument.h, shell/mainwindow_p.cpp, (...)
Load Kate part and work with it and its views in the same way kate does: 1)
use the factory only once and get one KTextEditor::Editor per KDevelop
instance (should speed up document creations because we won't ask trader to
get the same thing again and again) 2) use that editor's createDocument() to
create KTextEditor::Document without any views (before that we always created
a kate view together with kate part which could give us shortcut clashes,
visible toplevel views and so on) 3) explicitly ask for KTextEditor::View
creation using document->createView() to get views with correct parent
(like in unfamous rev.799888 4) when activating kate views plug and unplug
kate xmlgui manually because each kate view is a guiclient and our part
controller won't do the plugging/unplugging for us because kate views
obviously belong to the same part CCMAIL: kdevelop-devel@kdevelop.org

Just found a nice thread on the qt-interest list that queued connections work
automatically, without the need for any "helper" object that lives in the
non-gui-thread. So remove all the helper classes and simply emit the signals

2008-03-16 03:02 +0000 [r786083] David Nolden <david.nolden.kde art-master.de>
language/duchain/topducontext.cpp
Completely remove the (unreliable) imports-cache, and instead manage exact
connectivity information that at any time stores the shortest path from each
top-context to all the ones that it imports at any level. This brings quite a
performance-penalty when fiddling around with imports in very complex import
structures, but it is CORRECT, so updating will be more reliable. It is mainly
so complex because we allow loops in the import-structure. But the most
important thing: This fixes the "undebuggable" crash I mentioned on the
mailing list, which actually was infinite recursion in
TopDUContext::importTrace.

2008-03-04 17:29 +0000 [r782250] Robert Knight <robertknight gmail.com>
plugins/duchainviewer/duchainmodel.cpp
Fix a crash when expanding contexts in the DUChain Viewer because the internal
pointer for the index representing the same top level DUContext could be
different depending on how it was created (using parent() which created it
with createPointerForObject() or versus createIndex() which used
&m_chain). This caused a crash in QTreeViewPrivate::layout() when the
stored index for the top level context was not equal to the one obtained by
navigating up the index hierarchy from the currently expanded item. Fix this
by using createPointerForObject() to create the index in createIndex().
CCMAIL: zwabel@googlemail.com

2008-02-24 11:19 +0000 [r778694] Andreas Pakulat <apaku gmx.de>
sublime/CMakeLists.txt,

2008-02-23 23:48 +0000 [r778610] David Nolden <david.nolden.kde art-master.de>
language/duchain/ducontext.cpp,
language/duchain/smartconverter.cpp,
language/duchain/definitions.h,
plugins/classbrowser/classtree.cpp, language/CMakeLists.txt,
language/duchain/duchainpointer.h, (...)
ContextOwner was only needed because of Definition, and pure Definitions do
not make sense because: - Declarations sometimes are definitions anyway - For
global functions, sometimes a definition should be interpreted as a
declaration at the same time, while still mapping to a pure declaration in a
header. - Definitions did not store comments and potentially other useful
information. - Parsing definitions represented as a separate class was quite
painful in C++ support. - Separate definitions made the code more complex. So
from now on, definition and declarations are always represented by
"Declaration", and separate definition/declaration mapping happens through the
"definition()" and "declaration()" functions.

2008-02-22 01:25 +0000 [r777977] David Nolden <david.nolden.kde art-master.de>

2008-02-22 01:16 +0000 [r777974] David Nolden <david.nolden.kde art-master.de>
language/duchain/ducontext.cpp,
language/duchain/smartconverter.cpp, language/duchain/uses.cpp
(added), language/duchain/duchain.h, language/CMakeLists.txt,
language/duchain/ducontext.h, (...)
Completely rework the way uses are stored and attached to their declarations.
1. Make uses extremely memory-efficient by reducing each use to 5 integers
stored in a vector(range + declaration-index). 2. Manage the uses locally
within the context that contains them, and hold a parallel vector that
eventually contains smart-ranges when available. That way we lose no memory
for the 99.99% uses that don't have smart-ranges. 3. Like done with
definitions, use an intermediate structure that uses the declaration-id for
the mapping from declarations to uses. That way, we will never get problems
from documents parsed in multiple versions, the declarations all share the
same uses. Now we can actually start thinking about building uses for all
parsed files(If it just was faster).

2008-02-16 21:20 +0000 [r775955] Andreas Pakulat <apaku gmx.de>
shell/project.cpp, shell/project.h, interfaces/iproject.h
change the interface to get a project item for a url. This implementation is a
lot slower than the old one, however the old one was incorrect in two ways: -
it assumed there's only 1 project item for a given url, thats wrong as a file
might be part of multiple targets - it assumed that the project item for a
given url is inside the subtree that has the same path, which might not be the
case In the cause of this, the function now returns a list of items, that is
all these items have the same url, but different parents. The language support
parts probably want to do something more sensible than just taking the first
one. CCMAIL:kdevelop-devel@kdevelop.org

2008-01-24 18:42 +0000 [r765814-765815] David Nolden <david.nolden.kde art-master.de>
plugins/usehighlight/usehighlight.cpp
language/interfaces/ilanguagesupport.cpp (added),
language/interfaces/ilanguagesupport.h
use ILanguageSupport::standardContext to retrieve the context that is used for
use-highlighting.
Add a new function ILanguageSupport::standardContext(...) that is intended to
return the default context to use for things like navigation,
use-highlighting, etc. if there is multiple versions of a parsed file. The

2007-12-22 14:48 +0000 [r751649] David Nolden <david.nolden.kde art-master.de>
language/duchain/ducontext.cpp,

Completely change the way forward-declarations work. Statically resolving them
while building the du-chain simply is incompatible with re-using pre-compiled
du-chains. So make forward-declarations dynamically resolvable, using a given
top-context as visibility hint. In Declaration: Make the behavior of
"internalContext" simpler, and add virtual convenience-functions
"logicalInternalContext" and "logicalDeclaration" that resolve everything on
the way.

2007-12-20 16:19 +0000 [r750937] David Nolden <david.nolden.kde art-master.de>

2007-12-20 12:38 +0000 [r750890] Hamish Rodda <rodda kde.org>

2007-12-20 02:27 +0000 [r750765] David Nolden <david.nolden.kde art-master.de>
language/duchain/ducontext.cpp,
language/duchain/smartconverter.cpp,
editor/documentrangeobject.h,
language/duchain/forwarddeclaration.h,
language/duchain/namespacealiasdeclaration.h,
plugins/classbrowser/classtree.cpp, (...)
Profiling has shown that DocumentRange was one of the biggest remaining
memory-hogs, especially on 64-bit systems KTextEditor::Range takes much more
memory than the actual content because the data is split across multiple
separately allocated blocks. Also, it is inefficient to copy around, and
DocumentRanges maintain a hierarchy that isn't needed at all, but also takes a
lot of memory. Solution: Create efficient self-contained classes SimpleRange
and SimpleCursor, that are used for each duchain object. Stop using
DocumentRange in DocumentRangeObject. Instead, now each duchain object has one
permanently stored SimpleRange, and a SmartRange pointer that is only nonzero
when the document is loaded and has a smart-range. The SimpleRange and the
SmartRange are synchronized on access. Result: - No more thread-unsafe range
access in DocumentRangeObject::textRange() - Significantly less memory
consumption - More efficient serializability because the SimpleRange is
embedded in the shared d-pointer. By the way the duchain initializations were
cleaned up a little, and some yet unnoticed bugs there fixed.

during parsing and using the duchain. Solution: Change DocumentRangeObject to
use HashedString, which allows lighting fast comparison. This also solves the
problems about thread-unsafety and deep-copying in KUrl. Port everything to
that change.

sure no output from the process is lost. Change the const char* to QByteArray,

2007-11-22 23:11 +0000 [r740306] Andreas Pakulat <apaku gmx.de>
plugins/projectmanagerview/projectmanagerviewplugin.cpp
Here's a really subtle bug: Create a toolviewfactory and add it to the Ui in
the plugin constructor. Then later in the constructor create something that
the toolview will use. This works fine when the plugin is loaded during
kdevelop startup (i.e. in this case when projects from a previous session are
reloaded), but it breaks when the plugin is loaded in an already running
kdevelop (i.e. no projects reloaded and you open one). Fix is of course easy,
move the toolview stuff to the end of the constructor, still I think we should
find out why it breaks in one case and not the other and see if we can fix
that. CCMAIL:kdevelop-devel@kdevelop.org

2007-10-24 13:08 +0000 [r728852] Oswald Buddenhagen <ossi kde.org>
shell/partcontroller.cpp, shell/project.cpp
KConfig* API overhaul. only cosmetics, so don't panic. KConfigBase: - remove
separator argument from list entry reading/writing functions - introduce
{read,write}XdgListEntry() - kill readPathListEntry(), add readPathEntry()
overload instead. the default value is not optional any more, as it defines
the return type. this is consistent with the readEntry() functions. - rename
clean() => markAsClean(), remove rollback() - rename ConfigState =>
AccessMode, getConfigState() => accessMode() - rename
{entry,group}IsImmutable() => is{Entry,Group}Immutable() - remove NLS alias
to Localized KConfig: - remove setGroup() & group() - reshuffle OpenFlag
enum, introduce NoCascade for symmetry - remove setExtraConfigFiles() alias to
addConfigSources() KConfigGroup: - inherit KConfigBase::deleteGroup()
overloads - make convertToQVariant() private, it will probably change somehow
- KConfig & KConfigGroup: deprecate entryMap() - remove bogus
declarations: KConfigGroup::setReadDefaults(),
KConfig::readEntryUntranslated() - apidox - reshuffle the declarations in the
headers

2007-08-15 18:50 +0000 [r700516] David Nolden <david.nolden.kde art-master.de>
language/duchain/ducontext.cpp, language/duchain/symboltable.cpp,
language/duchain/smartconverter.cpp,
language/duchain/topducontext.cpp,
language/duchain/ducontext_p.h,
language/duchain/namespacealiasdeclaration.h, (...)
1. Change the symbol-table to not work with strings, but instead with the
hashes that are stored within QualifiedIdentifiers. 2. Change
QualifiedIdentifiers to not store strings directly, but instead only contain a
list of sub-identifiers plus a hash-value. For normal usage the hash-values
and sub-identifiers are everything that is needed. This may greatly improve
speed and reduce memory-consumption. Add some convenience-functions, and make
QualifiedIdentifiers ignore the explicitly-global mark while comparison. 3.
Rewrite the namespace-importing and aliasing system. A namespace-alias or
import now is represented by a NamespaceAliasDeclaration. That allows
accessing them efficiently from the outside using the symbol-table. Implement
a working namespace-aliasing and -importing system on top of that, that
supports local imports/aliases as well as global imports from headers, etc. 4.
Many small fixes.

2007-08-09 03:13 +0000 [r698086] David Nolden <david.nolden.kde art-master.de>
editor/editorintegrator.cpp, editor/editorintegrator.h
1. When creating a Range as a slave of another Range, and there already is a
slave-range that contains the added one, move the added down into that range.
2. If there is Ranges that are contained by the added one, move them into the
added one. Without this, the ranges get crippled up to non-functionality. This
solves a lot of problems in C++ support, makes the code-highlighting and
declaration-search work better, and will help fixing the du-chain updating.
It's not 100% clean though, we can talk about another solution. This little
patch is the result of a whole day of debugging. :)

2007-07-27 21:03 +0000 [r693388] David Nolden <david.nolden.kde art-master.de>
language/duchain/ducontext.cpp,
language/duchain/topducontext.cpp,
language/duchain/duchainpointer.h,
language/duchain/ducontext_p.h, language/duchain/ducontext.h,
language/duchain/duchainlock.cpp, (...)
1. Do not allow acquiring of du-chain write-locks when read-locks are held 2.
Change the du-chain so the C++ language part is able to instantiate
template-specializations with only a read-lock held. This means: - Allow
arbitrary writing to du-chain-items that are not attached to the du-chain, and
thus not reachable for other threads. - Make DUContext::addDeclaration not
require a read-lock by using a mutex that protectes the local declaration from
simultaneous access. 3. Remove the addAnonymous... members. They were not
needed. Instead, anonymous du-chain items must be destroyed separately(in the
c++ case, they are destroyed by the items they were specialized from). Allow
contexts and declarations to be added anonymously in a way that there is no
what-so-ever connection from their parent-context to them.

2007-07-25 01:22 +0000 [r692088] David Nolden <david.nolden.kde art-master.de>
language/duchain/ducontext.cpp, editor/documentrangeobject.h,
language/duchain/classfunctiondeclaration.cpp,
language/CMakeLists.txt, language/duchain/identifier.cpp,
language/duchain/ducontext.h, (...)
1. Allow declarations and child-contexts being added anonymously into
contexts. This is used for specialized template-classes that should not be
directly accessible. 2. Correctly handle identifiers: An identifier's
template-arguments were always lost when put into a QualifiedIdentifer before.
Now Identifier can automatically parse template-arguments from a string like
"A<B,C>", and arguments never get lost. 3. Make the du-chain locking
mechanisms completely recursive. Now you can lock the du-chain as many times
as you wish, in any order(first read-lock, then write-lock, opposite, etc.).
Btw. also solve some other locking-problems. 4. Add & implement new
virtual clone() and exchangeTypes(..) functions in the type-system. Those are
used to instantiate template-specialized versions of types. Also add a
simplified type-visitor and visitor for exchangeTypes(..). 5. Allow changing
the ownership of the document-ringe in DocumentRangeObject.(Is needed so
template-instantiations can share the range with the original)

implementation of two other parts, and is not needed for every single du-chain

Add a new pointer-system for du-chain items that allows pointers that
invalidate themselves, at the cost we saved by removing the duchainbase
d-pointer. This is needed because du-chain items may get deleted whenever the
du-chain is unlocked, and monitoring the du-chain for that is inconvenient in
many cases.
